<snip>

I worked for the federal govermnent for 15 years and then worked about 3.5 
years in private industry.  I was working as a contractor at my agency when 
they asked me to become a government employee.  I returned at the top step 
of my grade and have worked here for a little over 19 years.  By leaving for 
private industry I got to the top step of my grade faster, but for the last 
19 years I have only received cost of living increases. Nevertheless my 
salary more than doubled during the last 19 years.  I did not like the way 
the system worked when I was a contractor.  My employer would get as big an 
increase from my agency as they could and the they would try to give me as 
little of it as possible and keep the rest for themselves.  I never could 
find out the exact figures.

I have decided to retire and August 1, 2011 will be my last day.  I think I 
am getting out just in time.  They are planning a reorganization from hell 
that will never work in my opinion.  Everyone will be placed in a pool and 
then be assigned to projects.  People on projects will be colocated so as 
projects change they must move around.  In my opinion the subsystems are 
each extremely complicated and unless you work on one for quite a while you 
will have trouble understanding all of the intricate details and 
interdependencies with other subsystems.  They call it matrix management. 
Yuck!
```

It is also called 'project-driven management' and completely ignores the

(according to some theories there is a different between 'functional 
work', ie 'that which is done every day', and a 'project', a task with 
defined beginning and end and producing an unique product.  the ultimate 
Corner-Office Idiot conclusion is to make each functional task a project, 
eg every order which comes in is not an order to be filled, a function of 
the Order-Processing Department (a department has associated overhead and 
fixed costs, bad, bad, bad) but each and every order is its own 'project', 
producing an unique product)

>Yuck! 

Almost prescient, I'd say.

DD

```
Charles Hottel wrote:
> "SkippyPB" <swiegand@Nospam.neo.rr.com> wrote in message
> news:in2627pbe1q7sbj099vvop8ue88t6n7vpl@4ax.com...
…[153 more quoted lines elided]…
> management. Yuck!

The idea of matrix management (nothing to do with Neo...) is to spread the 
risk by getting a better skills portfolio and to cut through some of the 
rigid hierarchies that stifle organizations.

The downside is that in-depth expertise gets diluted,  people are less happy 
at being functionally and physically moved about, and there is little direct 
responsibility for anything. It can work (I saw it work in ONE place) but it 
needs a special kind of organizational culture (which is generally not found 
in Government Agencies) to be really successful.

If you fancy a side bet I'll bet you a beer against a JD that it is thrown 
out within 2 years. (In a commercial organization it would last about 9 
months, but Government is more ponderous. :-))

Pete.
```

```
HeyBub wrote:
> Alistair Maclean wrote:
>> On Jul 12, 8:31 pm, "HeyBub" <hey...@NOSPAMgmail.com> wrote:
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
> I didn't know.

:-)

This made me think. In all my experience I don't remember a single female 
mainframe computer operator. I worked with female programmers (some of whom 
were very good indeed) but Operations seemed to be reserved for males. I 
think it was because the machines were so expensive and the general wisdom 
at the time was that women couldn't be trusted to remain calm if a crisis 
arose :-)

Social Security stops sending money all the time.  The SSA has disability

for children that kids grow out of.

## Thread: Newbie - Fujitsu Cobol question — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers) · [`Tutorials, books, learning`](topics.md#learning)_

### Newbie - Fujitsu Cobol question

- **From:** zalek <zalekbloom@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-13T07:49:29-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<330f43d7-77c8-4b7f-851c-54a72a62aa1b@m18g2000vbl.googlegroups.com>`

```
We are running Fujitsu Cobol from a DOS screen.
Is it possible to write a Fujitsu Cobol command which will display a
text on this screen?
I tried DISPLAY 'aaa' upon console, display 'aaa' upon sysout and
display 'aaa' upon syserr, but each time it opened new screen.
What I want is the display on the same screen - so it will look like
it came from the ECHO command.

Thanks.

Zalek
```

#### ↳ Re: Newbie - Fujitsu Cobol question

- **From:** Alistair Maclean <alistair.j.l.maclean@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-13T10:54:08-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<5b952bf5-63aa-4edc-9786-3952e4ca40e9@x10g2000vbl.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<330f43d7-77c8-4b7f-851c-54a72a62aa1b@m18g2000vbl.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Jul 13, 3:49 pm, zalek <zalekbl...@hotmail.com> wrote:
> We are running Fujitsu Cobol from a DOS screen.
> Is it possible to write a Fujitsu Cobol command which will display a
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> Zalek

You could try:

(from the Fujitsu manual) Environment variable information
@CBR_CONSOLE = COBOL
may be specified with the compiler option MAIN (MAIN). In this
case, when an application is started using a method other than
input to the command prompt window, such as by clicking an
icon, a system console is generated soon. In addition, a COBOL
console is also generated for input-output use.
```

#### ↳ Re: Newbie - Fujitsu Cobol question

- **From:** "tleaders...gmail.com" <tleaders@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-13T11:10:13-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e457c90b-ca2f-44c4-a974-ccd426f42ac7@f35g2000vbr.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<330f43d7-77c8-4b7f-851c-54a72a62aa1b@m18g2000vbl.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Jul 13, 10:49 am, zalek <zalekbl...@hotmail.com> wrote:
> We are running Fujitsu Cobol from a DOS screen.
> Is it possible to write a Fujitsu Cobol command which will display a
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> Zalek



Zalek

A lot is going to depend on which compiler you have. Fujitsu is giving
away version 3 and selling version 10? also there are .Net compiler
versions that match each on the Microsoft .NET versions. So with that
in mind.

This program

000010 PROGRAM-ID. HELLO.
000010 PROCEDURE DIVISION.
000010     DISPLAY "HELLO BACK".
000010     STOP RUN.

When compiled with this batch file.

CALL "COBOLC.EXE" %1.CBL /WC:SRF(FIX,FIX) /TARGET:EXE /MAIN:%1 /PRINT:
%1.ERR


Looks like this:
C:>hello
HELLO BACK


Good luck
Tom
```

## Thread: COBOL News groups — 23 msgs

_Topics: [`Meta: FAQs, group policy, charter`](topics.md#meta)_

### COBOL News groups

- **From:** Cheryl Watson <cheryl@watsonwalker.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-14T06:12:27-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<50e9d259-056c-4e97-b7b7-591b4955d05e@y13g2000yqy.googlegroups.com>`

```
I joined this group to brush up on my COBOL skills, but I see more OT
topics than COBOL topics. Are there other groups for COBOL topics, or
is (as someone mentioned) the language dying and there is little
interest in sharing techniques or information?

I'd appreciate any information as to other sources if there are any.

Many thanks!
(From a woman who programmed COBOL in 1967!)
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL News groups

- **From:** Kerry Liles <"kerry.liles[minus_the_spam]"@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-14T09:28:21-04:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ivmqul$3cg$1@dont-email.me>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<50e9d259-056c-4e97-b7b7-591b4955d05e@y13g2000yqy.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<50e9d259-056c-4e97-b7b7-591b4955d05e@y13g2000yqy.googlegroups.com>`

```
On 7/14/2011 9:12 AM, Cheryl Watson wrote:
> I joined this group to brush up on my COBOL skills, but I see more OT
> topics than COBOL topics. Are there other groups for COBOL topics, or
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> (From a woman who programmed COBOL in 1967!)

You are not the only one who has noticed the signal to noise ratio here, 
but there are some nuggets occasionally. If something is marked "OT" it 
isn't necessarily off topic, but huge portions of it may be...

If you have specific questions, post them here and I am sure you will 
get reasonable replies (and I am equally certain the thread might get 
hijacked into OT land at some point).

You may have better luck just using Google or Bing to search for 
specific information (especially if you can qualify the search with 
product names and version numbers, or with case-specific keywords like 
"CICS" - just to pick one at random).

Hope this helps a little.

Kerry
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL News groups

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-07-15T02:31:34+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<988cu8F47lU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<50e9d259-056c-4e97-b7b7-591b4955d05e@y13g2000yqy.googlegroups.com> <ivmqul$3cg$1@dont-email.me>`

```
Kerry Liles" <"kerry.liles[minus_the_spam] wrote:
> On 7/14/2011 9:12 AM, Cheryl Watson wrote:
>> I joined this group to brush up on my COBOL skills, but I see more OT
…[24 more quoted lines elided]…
> Kerry

A very good response, Kerry.

I'm not sure I agree about the signal to noise ratio because my definition 
of "signal" is anything interesting, rather than how to structure 
redefinitions in COBOL or the intricacies of using UNSTRING with pointers, 
as a couple of examples. (These things may be interesting, especially if you 
are having a problem with them, and then they become "signal"... but there 
are many really interesting things discussed here and for some time now the 
OT posts have been much more interesting than the COBOL ones, in my 
opinion.)

Although it may have started out as a purely COBOL newsgroup, it is an 
unmoderated forum and, as such, is a useful place for people to say what 
they think, not just about COBOL, but about most things.

I see it as a group of interesting people who share a common interest in 
COBOL.

But in fairness to people who may come here only for COBOL I think more care 
should be taken in marking topics OT.

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL News groups

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-07-15T02:20:09+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<988c8sFuniU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<50e9d259-056c-4e97-b7b7-591b4955d05e@y13g2000yqy.googlegroups.com>`

```
Cheryl Watson wrote:
> I joined this group to brush up on my COBOL skills, but I see more OT
> topics than COBOL topics. Are there other groups for COBOL topics, or
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> (From a woman who programmed COBOL in 1967!)

A search of the USENET newsgroups for the word COBOL returns a handful, but 
most of them are not very active.

The largest group would be the IBM listsrv group which is showing over 
12,000 posts on my system. (You will be required to subscribe to this group 
and it is NOT a COBOL group as such, although IBM COBOL does get discussed 
there.)

Here in comp.lang.cobol specific questions about COBOL usually do get 
answered  but there is not much non-specific discussion on COBOL,. Maybe 
because the group has been running for years and the regulars here have said 
most of what they want to say about COBOL. :-) The language has not had any 
major innovations for quite some time so there hasn't been that much to 
discuss.

There is no problem with sharing techniques or information, but you will 
need to ask for what you want or start a topic on what you are interested 
in.

There is a COBOL forum dealing with specific problems in specific COBOLs at 
the COBOL User Group (COBUG), and Micro Focus run a similar forum in support 
of their COBOL products.

If you are interested in looking at modern Object Oriented COBOL or seeing 
how to lever standard procedural COBOL into OO COBOL, plus a number of free 
tools and examples, have a look at the COBOL21 site: 
http://primacomputing.co.nz/cobol21
(You can comment here on anything you see there and there is a direct link 
from that site back to this forum on most pages of it.)

As for programming in COBOL in 1967.... Snap! so did I...:-)

Pete.
```

On 14 Jul., 20:21, Cheryl Watson <che...@watsonwalker.com> wrote:
> Thanks so much for the references. I assume the IBM listsrv group you
> mentioned is IBM-Main. Yes, I slog through that every day, and the OT
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Cheryl,

I looked at the presentations you provided the links for and the one
about the performance was interesting for me.

When I started programming in the early 70's, this was on a Unisys
9400 system using the assembler language. Performance was a very
important requirement and the CPU usage and I/O performance was as
important as the correct functioning.

Later on, when COBOL was the main language I used, performance
considerations had still their place in how I implemented code. In the
mid 90's we had a larger migration project from a Unisys system 80 to
a decent Unix system and I was running a batch program for an inital
test. While the program took one hour on the mainframe, it completed
in a bit less than a minute on the Unix system. This was when I
decided that performance  is not going to have the same importance for
me as it used to have.

I'm not saying, that performance it is not important, but the focus
had changed for me. These days however, mainframe usage is charged by
CPU usage in some licensing models, so it might change again.

Regards Hans
```

Welcome to UseNet, where the signal-to-noise ratio is what it gets made to 
be.  Being an older technology (some have described UseNet as 'the same 
old farts twenty-five years later' or something) it attracts mostly older 
folks and this group appears to be no exception; most of the contributions 
made over the past decade are made by the same, apparently-diminishing 
group of folks.

(Oh... speaking of the 'same... group of folks' a fellow who used to post 
here and may still work here, Mr Rayhawk, ran into someone I know at a 
recent contract they both worked on in Maryland.  The closer one gets to 
the top of a pyramid the smaller the cross-section.)

Now where was I?  Oh, yes, that stuff the kids're listening to nowadays... 
they call that *music*?  Buncha durned noise, 'f'ya ask me... and another 
thing...

... oh yes, this, being UseNet, relies on contributions... and by that I 
mean a non-moderated newsgroup (such as this one is) gets shaped by what 
folks post.  Want to learn something?  Do a bit of research and ask a 
question, eg 'I've been wondering about flesh-eating bacteria as a weapon 
of war but under (compiler, operating-system - not all are the same) when 
I code MOVE SARS TO FIELD-OF-WAR I get a high-level error and the message 
of 'ABCDE01234-* ACTION PROHIBITED BY CURRENT GENEVA PROTOCOLS'.  Any idea 
what I'm doing wrong?'

(doing otherwise might lead to some postings of moderate assistance, some 
of moderate derision and perhaps even one laconic 'Please do your own 
homework.')

>Are there other groups for COBOL topics, or
>is (as someone mentioned) the language dying and there is little
>interest in sharing techniques or information?

The answer on that, as with many things, depends on whom one asks.

DD

> bill

I have been in LinkedIn almost since it started. It is the ONLY "social 
network" I am in.

I joined it because some people who had worked for me asked if I would 
recommend them.

There has been very little effort involved and very little time so, for me 
at least, it has NOT been a "complete waste of time and effort".

However, it has moved during the last few years to become more of a social 
network than a professional one and that kind of defeats the purpose as far 
as I am concerned. I have never upgraded myself to a paying membership and 
have no intention to do so so. As it is free, I have no complaints about it. 
I do get emails from it telling me that people I am connected to have done 
something, but I have never made any attempt to expand my connections or 
"get involved". For the same reasons, I have not, and do not intend to, 
contribute to the groups on it (COBOL or otherwise).

A few years back I would have unhesitatingly recommended it as a very good 
professional network, useful for keeping in touch with past associates. 
Today I wouldn't do that, as it is little more than Facebook for 
Professionals.

Still as long as it is free and does not require significant effort, I have 
no beef with it.

Pete.

```
Bill Gunshannon wrote:
> In article <qo03379usooo4dqtjee051ml7thj8ct15a@4ax.com>,
> SkippyPB <swiegand@Nospam.neo.rr.com> writes:
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> bill

LinkedIn is neither small nor insignificant. (It has grown very quickly in 
the last couple of years.)

But that doesn't matter. I'm more concerned about the general darkness you 
seem to be seeing, Bill. :-)

The "Wasteland" of which you speak (presumably, the Internet?) is exactly 
what you make it. It has woven itself into the fabric of our lives and is 
continuing to do so. There are really cool things that this enables, and 
there is a load of old rubbish as well. :-)

Whether we like it or not, mobile devices and the Internet are changing the 
way we live and do business.

The same influences are changing the way we use computers and this is part 
of what has led to the demise of COBOL. It's just Evolution. Things change.

I know you've had some disappointment with COBOL job applications. Don't let 
it get you down. If you have your heart set on a COBOL job you will find 
one. It just takes time and it might involve having to move to where the job 
is.

In the meantime, you are perfectly placed in an organization to expand your 
skill set. It must be an interesting and stimulating environment. You'll 
probably miss it when you do move to a job in industry... :-)

I don't know if it helps, but you should know you are not alone. Many 
(possibly even "most"...) of us have been there.

The first COBOL job I ever got (after the place where I went on the COBOL 
course...), I made around 70 applications and never had exactly what they 
were looking for. (I was trying to move from ICL COBOL to IBM COBOL as, in 
those days, without IBM experience you had no career...) It is the old 
vicious circle; you don't have the experience they want and you can't get it 
unless they give you a job... In the end I managed to get a couple of 
interviews and I took sample listings of  working COBOL programs I had 
written along. I also told them I was happy to do anything they required 
(mop the floor, make the coffee...) as long as I could have access to the 
machine and the manuals for it so I could teach myself the Assembler. The 
guy who interviewed me was so impressed with my enthusiasm he employed me on 
the spot and I never looked back.

Don't let the darkness overwhelm you. Attitude has a lot to do with getting 
what you want... And remember that even if you can't change a condition, you 
can change your mind about the condition :-)

I hope something comes along for you soon; meantime, hang in there!

Pete.
```

<a id="t-71c2d49e4c"></a>
## Thread: Looking for COBOL Expertise — 9 msgs

### Looking for COBOL Expertise

- **From:** Cheryl Watson <cheryl@watsonwalker.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-14T11:45:11-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<262806d1-a2af-472b-81cf-076c735b2d54@gh5g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`

```
An additional reason that I joined this group is that we are looking
for some help from someone with current COBOL expertise. By current, I
mean familiar with some of the more recent features, such as
generating XML. I am somewhat hesitant to post what we need because of
the rather negative response received by the poster of the "Quick
COBOL Assignment Needed". So I hope this query will not result in the
same "don't be so lazy" type of responses.

But here's what we need, and if you can pass this along to someone who
can help, we'd appreciate it. Also, if you think there is a better
place to post this, please let us know.

We need some software written in z/OS COBOL, and our COBOL skills are
out of date. So we are looking for someone to help us. This isn't a
full-time, nor even a part-time job. It might be a one-time
assignment, but it might also turn into an on-going part-time support
job. We have dismissed Java, REXX, and assembler for a variety of
reasons, so COBOL is our first choice. All work can be done from your
home by linking into our IBM ISV test site located in Dallas. All
communication would be via phone and email. As an example, here are
some of the first items to be delivered:

1. Set up our test site with PROCs for compiling and linking COBOL,
with the most efficient options. That is, set up our testing
environment.

2. Help create an overall program flow for a product that we've
designed.

3. Create a skeleton program to perform the basic function (read a
complicated file and create XML output), but designed to later add
sections to parse parameters and create reports.

There is no specific time frame for this, although we're ready to get
started. If you are interested, please send your resume, time
availability (hours per week and when you might become available), and
pay requirements to us at admin@watsonwalker.com. If you have a sample
COBOL program of yours, we'd love to see it. Before we discuss
anything further with you, we would need you to sign a confidentiality
agreement.

Many thanks,
Cheryl Watson
Watson & Walker, Inc.
Sarasota, Florida
www.watsonwalker.com
```

#### ↳ Re: Looking for COBOL Expertise

> An additional reason that I joined this group is that we are looking
> for some help from someone with current COBOL expertise. By current, I
> mean familiar with some of the more recent features, such as

I have briefly seen the "recent feature ... generating XML" by
creating record definitions and don't see much point to it. It seems
inflexible and clumsy. XML should be generated using templates. The
program should neither know nor care that it is XML being output. This
should also mean that the program could also output HTML, CSV or
printed reports by simply choosing a different template.


> I am somewhat hesitant to post what we need because of
> the rather negative response received by the poster of the "Quick
> COBOL Assignment Needed". So I hope this query will not result in the
> same "don't be so lazy" type of responses.

That particular thread appeared to be 'do my homework'. You will
probably get a 'post your rates' response to this.


> But here's what we need, and if you can pass this along to someone who
> can help, we'd appreciate it. Also, if you think there is a better
…[34 more quoted lines elided]…
> Sarasota, Floridawww.watsonwalker.com
```

programmers, and VERY experienced assembler programmers. If you can
suggest a rate, I'll use it. What I *do* know is that we are looking
for a particular person with a LOT of knowledge about z/OS and heavy
COBOL experience. If we find someone that we like, their rate does not
matter. Is COBOL that different from other contractors who have a
standard billing rate for their services? As I said, we have used
several z/OS consultants (SAS, sysprogs, performance analysts, etc.)
in the past, and each had their own rate requirements. We are looking
for someone who has at least ten years experience working in a z/OS
environment, and probably a great deal more. We know these people come
at a premium. Rather than rate, I should have included the expertise
we're looking for, because we're willing to pay what the right person
requests. We are NOT looking for the lowest rate. The more experience
the better. Another key requirement is the ability to communicate well
via email and phone.

#### ↳ Re: free compilers

- **From:** David L <david.lee.lambert@acm.org>
- **Date:** 2011-07-23T06:28:02-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c41ddfcd-b3cf-4ab3-950e-e4fca8f1b556@en1g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<6_IUp.18001$g12.13640@newsfe20.iad>`

```
On Jul 17, 6:02 pm, "Sprechen Sie C++" <upyo...@hotmail.com> wrote:
> So what compilers are available these days that are free
>
> I know on Linux COB2C is an option
>
> but anything for .NET maybe?

Micro Focus is offering a 30-day free trial of their "Visual Cobol R4
2011" product. Not sure if a time-limited free trial is what you're
looking for, but:

http://blog.microfocus.com/try-visual-cobol-r4-now/1169/

On Linux "open-cobol" is another option, it's available as a
distribution-built Debian package and compiles very easily on RHEL or
Cygwin, probably available in Fedora and Gentoo these days too.  The
compiler is "cobc".
```

was later discovered they were Mossad agents. Nevertheless, relations with 
Israel are still friendly. (Apparently NZ passports are useful to spies 
because it is an innocuous country that doesn't generally raise alarm bells, 
and Kiwis travel extensively, so are legitimately found all over the place.

After the Israeli case, procedures for obtaining NZ passports were tightened 
and new smart chips which contain an encrypted digital image of the holder, 
that would be extremely difficult to forge, are now embedded in the 
passports. (These were trialled in NZ using American equipment which will 
probably be deployed in the US, as the trial here proved very successful. 
The chip pops up an image on the Customs console when it is scanned and the 
Operator can see if the photo in the passport, the image on the chip, and 
the person in front of them are one and the same. Countries that don't have 
the readers use the old way of comparing the photo with the person. 
Processing at Immigration is considerably reduced due to the chips 
automatically checking other information like DOB etc. instantly. The next 
step will be to build a device with metal arms that grabs you if you haven't 
paid your taxes...:-)

I also hold a European passport and they have barcode/OCR information that 
speeds up processing at Heathrow. As mine is nearly due to expire, it is 
very possible the UK have moved to smart technology also.

Tragically, a number of teenagers from a number of countries (mostly 
backpackers) were killed in Christchurch when their hostel was destroyed by 
the quake. Japan was one of the first countries to come and help us, partly 
because some of those teenagers were Japanese.

The aftershocks and aftermath of Christchurch are still continuing and it is 
a heartbreak to see the faces of the people who are still trying to deal 
with it. The whole country grieves with them. It has been like 911 for us. 
But some amazing things have come out of it as well , so I guess nothing is 
ever completely bad.


>
> Now, I knew an Australian lady who had an Aussie passport AND a Greek
> passport. I don't think she worked for the Australian secret service
> but if it makes me famous I will denounce her as a spy.

She probably lived in Melbourne. :-) I had some of the best Greek food I 
ever tasted (and I have visited Greece) in Melbourne. There is a large Greek 
community there and some of them are characters... :-) The next best would 
be North London (Hendon) where I had a memorable kleftiko... :-) In Greece, 
the best was calamari yiachni cooked to order in a little cafe in a village 
near Patros. I enjoy food and cooking so memorable meals stay with me...:-)

Pete.
```

Also figure in that sometimes bearing an Israeli passport is a death 
sentence, or some other kind of inconvenience. Several countries, Britain 
among them, will issue a "passport of convenience" upon suitable 
representation.

My company used to have several South Africans (back during apartheid days) 
working for us. It was fairly routine for our vice-president to send a 
letter to the local British Consulate in Houston which resulted in a UK 
passport being created for our employee. This enabled our employees to 
travel in regions hostile to South Africa, south Los Angeles for example.

Point is, there is no general requirement that the bearer of a passport be a 
citizen of the country issuing the document.

##### ↳ ↳ OT: Border control WAS: Re: Spy in New Zealand?!?

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-07-22T02:52:23+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<98qsp7F5t4U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<e287843c-a163-421a-9ff1-5caf4cb7bc48@h25g2000prf.googlegroups.com> <zsWdnQf6P8bYiLXTnZ2dnUVZ_uCdnZ2d@earthlink.com>`

```
HeyBub wrote:
> iNFO_rene wrote:
>> My usual Yahoo news browsing brings me to this news.
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
> passport be a citizen of the country issuing the document.

You may be confusing citizen and resident here, Jerry. There is no 
requirement that the bearer be resident in the country issuing the document.

Your South African may have been issued a British Commonwealth passport, 
(which looked exactly like a British passport except that page 3 of it did 
not have the words: "Holder has the right of abode in the United Kingdom." 
on it.). These passports allowed Commonwealth citizens to travel under the 
protection of  Great Britain, but did not allow them to live and work there. 
Many people from the sub-continent , and previous African colonies, held 
these passports and fought to get them upgraded to full British nationality, 
so they could work in the U.K.  (The passport reflects citizenship. In this 
case, "British Commonwealth citizenship").

Since the British Passport has been replaced by the standard European one 
I'm not sure what the status of Commonwealth passports is now. The rules 
change. There was a time when Australians and NZers could travel freely and 
live and work in either Australia opr NZ, without any kind of travel 
document being required. Passport control has had to be introduced because 
many immigrants were using one of these countries as a "back door" to get 
into the other one. (If your immigration to Australia was declined due to 
quotas being full, for instance, you could apply for NZ and then simply move 
to Australia. If you couldn't make the requisite points threshold for 
immigration into NZ you could apply for Oz then move to NZ, and so on. 
Nowadays it is very much tighter and passports are required for trans-Tasman 
travel.

(I remember an Australian Immigration official having a good laugh at my 
expense when I arrived in Sydney on one occasion, only to find that my NZ 
passport had expired a few days before. I then produced a current European 
one and it was found to have no Australian visa in it. The NZ one did not 
require a visa for Australia but the UK one did. He was pretty good natured 
about it as there was no doubt I was a Kiwi, but he ribbed me about being an 
"honorary Pom" for the duration of my visit. They issued a visa on the spot, 
which was pretty decent of them really.)

Generally, passports must reflect the citizenship of the bearer, 
irrespective of where they reside. I have dual British and NZ citizenship so 
I can hold a full British (European) passport as well as a NZ one. It means 
I can reside in Europe or NZ and, for tax purposes I must state where my 
primary residence is. (It is now NZ,  but for some time it was the UK and, 
for a shorter time Germany, and Spain.)

Obviously any kind of effective border control needs proper documentation 
that should be difficult to forge. "Smart" passport technology is a step in 
the right direction.

The old trick of getting a passport issued in the name of some child that 
died at a young age (Stonehouse MP in England was a famous example), no 
longer works in NZ. But with a population of just over 4 million it is a lot 
easier for us to implement these kinds of cross references and controls, 
than it is to do so into a population of 350 million.

Pete.
```

## Thread: Newbie - can Fujitsu Cobol issue a Dos SET command? — 8 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers) · [`Tutorials, books, learning`](topics.md#learning)_

### Newbie - can Fujitsu Cobol issue a Dos SET command?

- **From:** zalek <zalekbloom@hotmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-21T09:05:18-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<7b5fc0c5-023d-4094-acca-1024e36fae33@s17g2000yqs.googlegroups.com>`

```
We are running Fujitsu Cobol on PC from a DOS prompt. I need issue a
DOS command:
SET MY_ENV=ZALEKS_PC

Can I issue this command from a COBOL? How?

Thanks,

Zalek
```

#### ↳ Re: Newbie - can Fujitsu Cobol issue a Dos SET command?

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-07-21T11:49:24-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<121a15f5-08b8-43b8-a3b8-e03baa862fc9@j14g2000prn.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<7b5fc0c5-023d-4094-acca-1024e36fae33@s17g2000yqs.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Jul 22, 4:05 am, zalek <zalekbl...@hotmail.com> wrote:
> We are running Fujitsu Cobol on PC from a DOS prompt. I need issue a
> DOS command:
> SET MY_ENV=ZALEKS_PC
>
> Can I issue this command from a COBOL? How?

You may be able to do something like:

    CALL "system" USING "SET MY_ENV=ZALECS_PC" & LOW-VALUE

However, issuing this command is unlikely to actually be what you want
to do, in that it probably won't do what you think you want.

The COBOL way of changing the environment variables is:

     DISPLAY "MY_ENV"    UPON ENVIRONMENT-NAME
     DISPLAY "ZALECS_PC" UPON ENVIRONMENT-VALUE

You may need to have SPECIAL-NAMES entries to cater for this.

But, due to the way that environment variables work, you may find that
this is not what you want either. In particular if you did:

    C:> SETZALEC
    C:> SET

The setting that 'SETZALEC' did will not show in the 'SET' listing.
When you run a program it is given a copy of the current environment
and any changes made are discarded when the program ends.
```

#### ↳ Re: Newbie - can Fujitsu Cobol issue a Dos SET command?

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-07-22T15:35:03+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<98s9f8F7q5U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<7b5fc0c5-023d-4094-acca-1024e36fae33@s17g2000yqs.googlegroups.com>`

zalek wrote:
> We are running Fujitsu Cobol on PC from a DOS prompt. I need issue a
> DOS command:
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> Zalek

Put it in a batch file and execute it, if you want it to be permanent.

You can activate ANY application from Fujitsu COBOL, including batch files, 
by using the Windows API. (You may need to add an appropriate .lib file to 
the project.) There are probably examples on the Alchemy site. If not post 
here and I'll send you a code sample.

If you only want it for the duration of your application run, use ACCEPT and 
DISPLAY to set and fetch Environment variables, as described in Fujitsu 
docs.


Pete.

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Newbie - can Fujitsu Cobol issue a Dos SET command?

- **From:** Lee Unterreiner <uncobol@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-27T23:10:19-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e895509b-ebee-4e5f-a413-385fdabf2468@j37g2000prh.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<7b5fc0c5-023d-4094-acca-1024e36fae33@s17g2000yqs.googlegroups.com> <98s9f8F7q5U1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Changing the environment won't work from within a Fujitsu COBOL
program.

The runtime creates a copy of the existing environment when it starts
up and creates a new process.  That environment goes away when a STOP
RUN is encountered and the process is terminated.

The way to do it is to to start the cobol app from a batch file and
then have the batch file execute a second batch file (which you create
in the cobol app) after the cobol app finishes.

Lee
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Newbie - can Fujitsu Cobol issue a Dos SET command?

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-07-29T19:40:25+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<99f6fcFc8dU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<7b5fc0c5-023d-4094-acca-1024e36fae33@s17g2000yqs.googlegroups.com> <98s9f8F7q5U1@mid.individual.net> <e895509b-ebee-4e5f-a413-385fdabf2468@j37g2000prh.googlegroups.com>`

```
Lee Unterreiner wrote:

Hi Lee,

nice to see you are still around... :-)

> Changing the environment won't work from within a Fujitsu COBOL
> program.
>

It depends on how you go about it.


> The runtime creates a copy of the existing environment when it starts
> up and creates a new process.  That environment goes away when a STOP
> RUN is encountered and the process is terminated.

That is absolutely true, if you use the local EV space in the inherited 
environment to store your EV.

However, the Windows OS has a number of different spaces for EVs. There is 
the temporary local one which is part of the environment inherited and used 
by the COBOL run time, but there are also USER and SYSTEM spaces which have 
more permanency.

If you want the EV to persist, you need to store it in one of these spaces. 
One way (and it is the way I use) to accomplish that is by using a Windows 
Script File. (For people who haven't cottoned to it yet, Windows scripting 
has replaced the DOS Batch facility, is infinitely more powerful than the 
old Batch files, and kind of does what JCL Procedures do on mainframes.) 
Windows scripts are contained in .wsf or .wsh files and these are executable 
just like.bat files. In effect, these are the Batch files of today.)
>
> The way to do it is to to start the cobol app from a batch file and
> then have the batch file execute a second batch file (which you create
> in the cobol app) after the cobol app finishes.

That is certainly one way, although it is a little convoluted.

Until I moved off COBOL and thereby gained more detailed understanding of 
what CAN be done, I probably would have done it like that too.

Nowadays, I don't do it that way as it seems unnecessary to constrain apps 
into starting from a batch file and then spawn another, not to mention the 
internal logic that must be added to your COBOL app so it can write the 
batch file which will be started after it completes.

Better by far just to write the EV into a persistent area. No generation of 
batch files required, no requirement for your app to be started from a batch 
file (in fact the technique works fine for PowerCOBOL as well, where there 
is a GUI interface and starting from a batch file is not usual.)

I checked the Fujitsu docs and samples to see how they recommend doing this 
and it is pretty awful.

Fujitsu Sample32 uses the hideous "StartProcessA" API interface to execute 
the batch file and they give no example that people could use to get around 
the need to generate a DOS batch file for setting EVs. (You also need two 
different versions of the interface depending on whether you are passing 
parameters to the app or not - it is just silly, really.)

I am a fan of component based programming and it just so happens that the 
Windows OS comes with hundreds of components already programmed into it. 
There is a COM component for doing a ShellExecute and it is very much easier 
than trying to pretend you are a VB program and interface directly through 
the WinAPI to StartProcessA. The advantage of a COM component is that it can 
be easily invoked from both Micro Focus and Fujitsu COBOL

I have posted a new thread describing all of the above with sample code, for 
people who can use it.

Pete.
```

---

#### ↳ Re: Baby Linux

- **From:** Ken <klshafer@att.net>
- **Date:** 2011-07-29T08:30:26-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c42db6e4-db9c-493c-bf12-8ec23a1f93a3@s17g2000yqs.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<99c0unFsu7U1@mid.individual.net>`

```
On Jul 27, 10:47 pm, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
> I had to smile when I saw this. It brought back memories of a time when we
> had to configure the OS down to 4 - 6K so we had more room to run
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> "I used to write COBOL...now I can do anything."

Here's another alternative that I use...

I installed MKS Toolkit, an earlier version, namely 5.1, on my
desktop, then copied over the binaries and the man pages to a cd-rom.
It was on the order of 16MB. (Yes, once again, like Baby Linux, that
is 16MB, not 16GB :-) )

I wrote a tiny .bat file based upon the MKS install that sets a
handfull of environment variables, like PATH, to point the binaries
and the /etc man pages, then invoked the shell (sh).

For those who prefer the command line and $ prompt this works quite
well. Because I execute the binaries off the cd-rom, I never actually
"installed" the software on the client machine. This is a useful
workaround when dealing with corporate bureaucracy.

Sadly, it breaks under Win 7, unless you invoke XP compatability mode
(which I was unable to do). However, it works great under Windows XP.
I would have used a memory stick (I did for a while) but I ran across
the corporate policy that memory sticks were verboten. Mr. Executive
VP was afraid we would download valuable organizational data. However,
the CD-ROM drives were READ-ONLY, which is all you need to invoked the
binaries. I made sure that my "working directory" was on the c: drive
where the utilities would deposit their output results, in the form of
text files. Again, which did not constitute an "Install", since they
were only text files.

I did extensive source code analysis on millions of lines-of-code
using such a tactic.

Ken
```

<a id="t-10fe2c9f41"></a>
## Thread: Issuing DOS commands, running Batch files, setting Environment Variables to persist, and starting applications, from COBOL. — 4 this month / 6 total

### Issuing DOS commands, running Batch files, setting Environment Variables to persist, and starting applications, from COBOL.

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-07-29T20:42:41+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<99fa43F75lU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
A recent thread in this forum requested help with setting Environment 
Variables (EVs) from COBOL.

(Please see my response to Lee Unterreiner in the "Newbie - can Fujitsu 
COBOL issue a DOS SET command?" thread if any of the following confuses 
you...)

The trouble with using ACCEPT and DISPLAY is that the EVs do not persist. 
They are lost as soon as you issue a stop run.

Below is a Windows Script File (.wsf) which takes 2 parameters. Put this 
file either in the current directory or somewhere on the system path.
(The description below is from a viewpoint of Win XP, but the script works 
fine in Win 7 and Vista also, as long as you have the necessary Registry 
write priveleges.)

The parameters are a value pair representing the name of an EV and the value 
you want set in it.

So, if you wanted to set an EV called "MyTestEV" to a value of "My Test 
Value" you would type the following on a Command line:

setEV  MyTestEV "My Test Value"

If you now type a SET command you will NOT see the new EV. However, if you 
close the command box, re-open, and type SET again, you can see that the EV 
has indeed been created/updated, and it has persisted beyond the process 
that created it.

Had you used the Windows GUI to check the EVs you would have seen it 
instantly. (Start>Control panel> system> advanced tab: Environment 
Variables)

OK, here's the script code (don't worry if you don't understand what it 
does; all you have to do is execute it at a command prompt...):

' This script sets an Environment Variable on Windows systems
' On entry the first parameter contains the variable name and second 
contains the required value.
' The "USER" EVs are set permanently by this and will persist after the 
process completes.

' Author: Peter E. C. Dashwood  Date: July, 2011
'
<package>
<job>
<script language="VBScript">
dim EVName, EVValue
Set oArgs = WScript.Arguments
EVName=oArgs(0)
EVValue = oArgs(1)
Set WshShell = WScript.CreateObject("WScript.Shell")
Set objEnv = WshShell.Environment("User")
On Error Resume Next
objEnv(EVName) = EVValue
</script>
</job>
</package>

Cut and paste the above into a text file and call it: setEV.wsf  You have 
now created yourself a new command line command called "setEV"

Once you are satisfied that it works, the next step is to call it from 
COBOL.

There are a number of ways to activate things from COBOL. Sadly most of the 
examples posted use the Win API directly and document for VB or C++. The 
example below uses the COM interface which is availabe in both Fujitsu and 
Micro Focus COBOLs. (The code is necessarily a little different between the 
two COBOLs, as Micro Focus does not use an intermediate COM handling Class 
and Fujitsu does (*COM). Nevertheless, it is a lot easier to create a COM 
object and invoke methods on it in either of these COBOLs, than it is to 
interface to the "StartProcessA" API function with the complex structures it 
requires.

Here is the Fujitsu version of the code:
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 @OPTIONS ALPHAL(WORD)
 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
 PROGRAM-ID. SetEVs.
*
*  This program demonstrates the use of the Windows Shell
*  component, which is a much easier way to
*  execute applications from COBOL than using the StartProcessA
*  Windows API function. You can start ANY executable using
*  this component, including Batch files, Scripts, and other
*  applications.
*
*  In this example, a Windows Script File is being used to
*  set a persistent Environment Variable. You can dynamically
*  decide what EV you want and what value you want it to have.
*  When the COBOL program completes, the EV persists and can be
*  referenced by any other processes.
*
*  Author: Peter E. C. Dashwood, July, 2011.

 ENVIRONMENT     DIVISION.
 CONFIGURATION SECTION.
 REPOSITORY.
     Class WinShell AS '*COM'.
*------------------------  DATA   DIVISION  -----------------
 DATA DIVISION.
 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
 01  ShellObj OBJECT REFERENCE WinShell.
 01  ShellProgID     pic x(30) value 'Shell.Application'.
 01  ShellReturn     pic s9(4) comp-5.
 01  parm1           pic x(15) value 'cscript.exe' & x'00'.
*> parm1 has the name of the executable you want.
 01  parm2           pic x(50) value spaces.
*> parm2 has the parameters you want passed to it.
 01  parm3           pic x value low-values.
 01  parm4           pic x(4) value 'open'.
 01  parm5           pic x value '1'.
 01  EVName          pic x(30).
 01  EVValue         pic x(50).
 PROCEDURE       DIVISION.
 Main Section.
 p000.
*
*> Set up the value pair (Name and value of the required EV), as two
*> parameters to the "setEV" Windows Batch file.
*>
*
     move "TestEV" to EVName *> these are an example; make it anything you 
like
     move "Value set from COBOL" to EVValue *> Note that the string may 
contain
                                            *> spaces.
*>
*> Build the command line as the second parameter to the Windows shell
*>
     move spaces to parm2
     string
          "setEV.wsf "          *> this will be the name of your Windows 
script
                                *> batch file
             delimited by size
          EVName
             delimited by space
          space
             delimited by size
          quote
             delimited by size
          EVValue
             delimited by "   " *> used 3 spaces as COBOL won't take ALL 
here
          quote
     delimited by size
          x'00'
             delimited by size  *> terminator for the value string
                into parm2
     end-string
*>
*> Ready to go... get a shell object from Windows...
*>

     invoke WinShell "CREATE-OBJECT" using ShellProgID
            returning ShellObj
     end-invoke
     invoke ShellObj "ShellExecute"
            using Parm1 *> Command to run..
                  Parm2 *> Parms to the Command...
                  Parm3 *> NULL
                  Parm4 *> 'open'
                  Parm5 *> '1'
        returning ShellReturn
     end-invoke
     set ShellObj to NULL
*>
*> Your EV is set into the USER EV area and saved in the Windows registry.
*>  It is there until you delete it and is available to any other processes.
*>
        .
 p999.
     exit program.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Clearly, if you change parm1 (The executable name) to be "cmd.exe" you can 
run DOS Batch commands (remember to put "/c" at the start of parm2). 
Similarly, you can put the name of ANY executable there and Windows will run 
it when you invoke the ShellExecute method of the COM component.

If you run an application that returns a completion code, Windows will put 
it into ShellReturn.

I hope this clarifies what can be a bewildering exercise in COBOL sometimes.

Pete.
```

:-)

#### ↳ Micro Focus COBOL version Re: Issuing DOS commands, running Batch files, setting Environment Variables to persist, and starting applications, from COBOL.

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-07-31T01:38:26+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<99ifqjF6o0U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<99fa43F75lU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Pete Dashwood wrote:
> A recent thread in this forum requested help with setting Environment
> Variables (EVs) from COBOL.
>
A full response using Fujitsu COBOL was posted but I was asked what changes 
would be needed  for this ot work in Micro Focus COBOL.

Here's the MF COBOL version:
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
        $set ooctrl(+P) mfoo
        IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
        PROGRAM-ID. SetEVs.
       *>
       *>  This program demonstrates the use of the Windows Shell
       *>  component, which is a much easier way to
       *>  execute applications from COBOL than using the StartProcessA
       *>  Windows API function. You can start ANY executable using
       *>  this component, including Batch files, Scripts, and other
       *>  applications.
       *>
       *>  In this example, a Windows Script File is being used to
       *>  set a persistent Environment Variable. You can dynamically
       *>  decide what EV you want and what value you want it to have.
       *>  When the COBOL program completes, the EV persists and can be
       *>  referenced by any other processes.
       *>
       *>
       *>  Author: Peter E. C. Dashwood, July, 2011.

        ENVIRONMENT     DIVISION.
        CONFIGURATION SECTION.
        CLASS-CONTROL.
            WinShell is class "$OLE$Shell.Application".
       *>------------------------  DATA   DIVISION  -----------------
        DATA DIVISION.
        WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
        01 ShellObj OBJECT REFERENCE.
        01 ShellProgID     pic x(30) value 'Shell.Application'.
        01 ShellReturn     pic s9(4) comp-5.
        01 parm1           pic x(15) value 'cscript.exe' & x'00'.
       *> parm1 has the name of the executable you want.
        01 parm2           pic x(50) value spaces.
       *> parm2 has the parameters you want passed to it.
        01 parm3           pic x value low-values.
        01 parm4           pic x(4) value 'open'.
        01 parm5           pic x value '1'.
        01 EVName          pic x(30).
        01 EVValue         pic x(50).
        PROCEDURE       DIVISION.
        Main Section.
        p000.
       *>
       *> Set up the value pair (Name and value of the required EV),
       *> as two
       *> parameters to the "setEV" Windows Batch file.
       *>
       *>
           move "TestEV" to EVName *> these are an example; make it
                                   *> anything you like
           move "Value set from COBOL" to EVValue *> Note that the
                                    *> string may contain spaces.
       *>
       *> Build the command line as the second parameter to
       *> the Windows shell
       *>
            move spaces to parm2
            string
                 "setEV.wsf "   *> this will be the name of your
                                *> Windows script
                                *> batch file
                    delimited by size
                 EVName
                    delimited by space
                 space
                    delimited by size
                 quote
                    delimited by size
                 EVValue
                    delimited by "   " *> used 3 spaces as COBOL
                                       *> won't take ALL here
                 quote
                    delimited by size
                 x'00'
                    delimited by size  *> terminator for the value
                       into parm2
            end-string
       *>
       *> Ready to go... get a shell object from Windows...
       *>

            invoke WinShell "New"  *> using ShellProgID
                   returning ShellObj
            end-invoke
            invoke ShellObj "ShellExecute"
                   using Parm1 *> Command to run..
                         Parm2 *> Parms to the Command...
                         Parm3 *> NULL
                         Parm4 *> 'open'
                         Parm5 *> '1'
               returning ShellReturn
            end-invoke
            set ShellObj to NULL
       *>
       *> Your EV is set into the USER EV area and saved in the
       *> Windows registry.
       *> It is there until you delete it and is available to
       *> any other processes.
       *>
           .
        p999.
            exit program.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
(As you can see, the changes are absolutely minimal from the Fujitsu 
original.)

You can build this code and either step through it or run it as an int or 
exe with the standard MF trigger.

It works. :-) (I have tested it. Remember to make sure the "setEV.wsf" file 
is on an executable path or in the same directory.)

The main points I'd like to make about this are as follows:

1. Windows has hundreds of useful components in it. You get them 
automatically when you buy the OS, so why not use them? It is really very 
easy to create an instance of the Windows Shell COM component and invoke the 
"ShellExecute" method of it. (See above). It is simple, clean, and elegant. 
Unlike the Sample provided by Fujitsu (I didn't check the MF ones), which 
uses the Win API and requires a dreadful interface. (To be fair, Fujitsu do 
provide sample code for the interface.)

2. It pays to find out more about things you want to do than is immediately 
obvious in COBOL. I never knew there were separate areas for EVs because 
COBOL only lets you use one of them (the local user area which is 
temporary). After using C# and becoming aware that setting and reading 
Registry values is a doddle (3 lines of code, including creating a registry 
object) it seemed reasonable to me that it should be possible to do these 
things with COBOL. It isn't ,because the COBOL runtime is static and uses 
its environment for storing EVs. (They are not pushed to the Registry for 
persistence).

3. Windows Script Hosting (the 21st century Batch file equivalent), gives 
you access to just about anything in Windows, including the Registry and the 
File System. You get an object instance of what you need and invoke whatever 
methods you want to use. The methods are well documented on Google and MSDN. 
You can add, change, delete directories and files before during and after 
running your COBOL, save application settings in the Registry, and much 
more. In fact, most of the stuff you CAN'T do with COBOL you can do FROM 
COBOL using WSH. (Personally, I find it easier to just give up COBOL 
altogether and use a language that lets me do everything, but YMMV...:-))

OK, so now you think you want to have a go at some of this? How can you find 
out what components are available? You need an OBJECT BROWSER. This will 
show you everything registered on your system as a COM (Component Object 
Model) component (including Automation components like Word, Excel, etc...) 
If you have MS Office installed there is an Object Browser that comes with 
Word Basic. Otherwise, there are free downloads. Failing that, you can 
browse the registry directly looking for COM registrations. I use something 
called COMExplorer but it is no longer available. If I run it on Windows XP 
SP3 it reports around 800 components. Some of them are extremely useful and 
can save you hours of work.

If you use either Micro Focus or Fujitsu COBOL to develop Windows 
applications, I would urge you to get into using components; it makes life 
much easier and it's actually fun :-)

Pete.
```

### Transfer file by XCOM from Mainframe to Unix

- **From:** "Jesus =)" <jecc86@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-29T08:33:24-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4fc8e298-7513-437f-8e1c-de5cca268f2e@q11g2000yqm.googlegroups.com>`

```
Hi
I need help you
I tried to transfer a file from mainframe to unix but i coudn't it
because the atributte FILE in my CTL is more greater than 72
characteres. My CTL is :
00001   IPFILE = xxxx.xxxx.xxxx.xxxx
00002   LFILE  =namearchive
00003   FILE = a path too long
00004   USERID="myuser"

I did this:

00001   IPFILE = xxxx.xxxx.xxxx.xxxx
00002   LFILE  =namearchive
00003   FILE = path
00004   FILE  =namefile.txt
00005   USERID="myuser"

but don't function, then I tried this

00001  IPFILE = xxxx.xxxx.xxxx.xxxx
00002  LFILE  =namearchive
00003  FILE = path                                          _
00004  FILE =namefile.txt
00005  USERID="myuser"

but don't function, then I tried this

00001  IPFILE = xxxx.xxxx.xxxx.xxxx
00002  LFILE  =namearchive
00003  FILE = path                                         &
00004  FILE = namefile.txt
00005  USERID="myuser"

I need to join the line 00003 and 00004 but i don't know how to do it
If someone know the answer, please send me
Thanks
```

## Thread: TAMIL ACTRESS HOT PHOTOS & VIDEOS — 1 msgs

### TAMIL ACTRESS HOT PHOTOS & VIDEOS

- **From:** gowri <gowri9030@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-07-30T08:02:39-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<e9a5adb7-19a7-4f14-82cf-530146197dfb@t8g2000prm.googlegroups.com>`

```


                FOR GOOD JOBS SITES TO YOU
                 http://goodjobssites.blogspot.com/

                                FOR HOT PHOTO&VIDEOS

                             KATRINA KAIF RARE PHOTOS
http://southactresstou.blogspot.com/2011/07/katrina-kaif-wallpapers.html
                    TAMANNA HOT SEXY PHOTOS & VIDEOS
http://southactresstou.blogspot.com/2011/07/tamanna-wallpapers.html
